When, how, and how much to retrain.\n\nResearch thoroughly:\n\n1. **Fixed schedule retraining** — retrain every N hours/days. What N works for 5-min crypto? Evidence from practitioners. The latency vs freshness tradeoff.\n\n2. **Performance-triggered retraining** — retrain when rolling Sharpe drops below threshold, or accuracy drops below X%. Threshold calibration. Avoiding retraining on every bad day.\n\n3. **Drift-triggered retraining** — retrain when feature distributions shift (PSI > threshold) or prediction distributions change. More principled than performance-based.\n\n4. **Warm-start vs cold-start retraining**:\n   - LightGBM: warm-start (init_model) vs full retrain. When does warm-start degrade?\n   - GRU: fine-tune (low LR) vs retrain from scratch. Documentation Discovery (Completed)\n     9→\n    10→### Verified APIs & Libraries\n    11→\n    12→**Exchange Data (ccxt pro)**\n    13→- `watch_order_book(symbol, limit)` — real-time L2 order book 19→**On-Chain Data (free, no auth)**\n    20→- mempool.space: REST + WebSocket (`wss://mempool.space/api/v1/ws`), `track-mempool` for streaming all new txs\n    21→- Blockchair: SQL-like filtering `?q=output_total(100000000..)` for whale detection (1,440 req/day free)\n    22→- blockchain.info: `/unconfirmed-transactions`, `/balance`, `/q/*` stats endpoints\n    23→- Alternative.me: Fear & Greed Index (`GET https://api.alternative.me/fng/`)\n    24→- Exchange inflow/outflow: NO free API exists — monitor known exchange addresses as workaround\n    25→\n    26→**Cross-Market Data**\n    27→- ETH: ccxt/Binance WebSocket (free, real-time, sub-100ms) — clear winner\n    28→- NQ/Gold/DXY historical: yfinance (`NQ=F`, `GC=F`, `DX-Y.NYB`) — 5-min bars, 15-min delayed, 60 days depth\n    29→- NQ/Gold near-real-time polling: Twelve Data (800 req/day free, `XAU/USD`)\n    30→- DXY: not available as native instrument anywhere free — must compute from forex components\n    31→\n    32→**ML Stack**\n    33→- XGBoost: `XGBClassifier`, incremental learning via `xgb_model=`, feature importance via `get_score(importance_type='gain')`\n    34→- PyTorch GRU: `nn.GRU(input_size, hidden_size, num_layers, batch_first=True)`, sequence length 12-60 steps\n    35→- HMM: `hmmlearn.GaussianHMM(n_components=3)`, no native online learning (use `init_params=\"\"` workaround)\n    36→- Optuna: `XGBoostPruningCallback` for XGB, `trial.report()`+`trial.should_prune()` for PyTorch\n    37→- Walk-forward: `sklearn.model_selection.TimeSeriesSplit(max_train_size=N)` for sliding window\n    38→- Feature engineering: `pandas-ta` (or `pandas-ta-classic` as fallback)\n    39→\n    40→### Anti-Patterns to Avoid\n    41→- Never random-split time series data\n    42→- Never use `bidirectional=True` on GRU (uses future data)\n    43→- Never run tsfresh in live prediction loop (offline feature discovery only)\n    44→- Never trust >70% directional accuracy without checking for look-ahead bias\n    45→- ccxt `binanceusdm` has intermittent WebSocket issues in v4.4.x — test your version\n    46→- Bybit order book via ccxt only supports depths [1, 50, 200, 1000] — slice from 50 for top-10\n    47→- hmmlearn is in maintenance mode — plan for potential migration\n    48→\n    49→---\n    50→\n    51→## Project Structure\n    52→\n    53→```\n    54→ep2-crypto/\n    55→├── pyproject.toml\n    56→├── PLAN.md\n    57→├── src/\n    58→│   └── ep2_crypto/\n    59→│       ├── __init__.py\n    60→│       ├── config.py                  # Settings, API keys, constants\n    61→│       ├── db/\n    62→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    63→│       │   ├── schema.py              # SQLite/TimescaleDB schema\n    64→│       │   └── repository.py          # Parameterized query layer\n    65→│       ├── ingest/\n    66→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    67→│       │   ├── base.py                # Base collector interface\n    68→│       │   ├── exchange.py            # Binance/Bybit klines, depth, trades\n    69→│       │   ├── derivatives.py         # OI, funding rate, liquidations\n    70→│       │   ├── onchain.py             # Mempool, whale txs, exchange addresses\n    71→│       │   ├── cross_market.py        # NQ, gold, DXY, ETH\n    72→│       │   └── orchestrator.py        # Manages all collectors\n    73→│       ├── features/\n    74→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    75→│       │   ├── base.py                # Feature pipeline interface\n    76→│       │   ├── microstructure.py      # Order book imbalance, trade flow, absorption\n    77→│       │   ├── onchain.py             # Whale flow, mempool pressure, exchange balance\n    78→│       │   ├── cross_market.py        # Lead-lag, correlation, divergence signals\n    79→│       │   ├── technical.py           # TA indicators (pandas-ta), volume features\n    80→│       │   ├── temporal.py            # Cyclical time encoding (sin/cos)\n    81→│       │   └── pipeline.py            # Combines all feature sets\n    82→│       ├── regime/\n    83→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    84→│       │   ├── detector.py            # HMM regime classification\n    85→│       │   └── labels.py              # Regime labeling utilities\n    86→│       ├── models/\n    87→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    88→│       │   ├── xgb_direction.py       # XGBoost direction classifier\n    89→│       │   ├── gru_magnitude.py       # GRU return magnitude predictor\n    90→│       │   ├── ensemble.py            # Regime-routed ensemble\n    91→│       │   └── tuning.py              # Optuna hyperparameter optimization\n    92→│       ├── backtest/\n    93→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    94→│       │   ├── walk_forward.py        # Walk-forward validation engine\n    95→│       │   ├── metrics.py             # Sharpe, drawdown, profit factor, accuracy\n    96→│       │   └── simulator.py           # Execution simulator with slippage/fees\n    97→│       └── api/\n    98→│           ├── __init__.py\n    99→│           └── server.py              # FastAPI prediction endpoint\n   100→├── scripts/\n   101→│   ├── collect_history.py             # Backfill historical data\n   102→│   ├── train.py                       # Full training pipeline\n   103→│   ├── backtest.py                    # Run backtests\n   104→│   └── live.py                        # Live prediction loop\n   105→├── tests/\n   106→│   ├── test_features/\n   107→│   ├── test_models/\n   108→│   ├── test_ingest/\n   109→│   └── test_backtest/\n   110→└── docker/\n   111→    ├── Dockerfile\n   112→    └── docker-compose.yml\n   113→```\n   114→\n   115→---\n   116→\n   117→## Phase 1: Foundation — Project Setup & Data Storage\n   118→\n   119→### What to implement\n   120→1. Initialize Python project with uv, configure `pyproject.toml` with all dependencies\n   121→2. Set up SQLite database with schema for: OHLCV candles, order book snapshots, trades, on-chain events, cross-market prices, regime labels\n   122→3. Build parameterized query repository layer (no string interpolation)\n   123→4. Set up structlog logging configuration\n   124→5. Create `config.py` with environment-variable-based settings (no .env files committed)\n   125→\n   126→### Dependencies\n   127→```toml\n   128→[project]\n   129→requires-python = \">=3.12\"\n   130→dependencies = [\n   131→    \"ccxt>=4.4\",\n   132→    \"websockets>=13.0\",\n   133→    \"pandas>=2.2\",\n   134→    \"numpy>=2.0\",\n   135→    \"xgboost>=2.1\",\n   136→    \"torch>=2.5\",\n   137→    \"hmmlearn>=0.3\",\n   138→    \"optuna>=4.0\",\n   139→    \"pandas-ta>=0.3\",\n   140→    \"scikit-learn>=1.5\",\n   141→    \"fastapi>=0.115\",\n   142→    \"uvicorn>=0.32\",\n   143→    \"structlog>=24.0\",\n   144→    \"httpx>=0.27\",\n   145→    \"aiosqlite>=0.20\",\n   146→]\n   147→```\n   148→\n   149→### Verification\n   150→- [ ] `uv run python -c \"import ep2_crypto\"` works\n   151→- [ ] Database creates tables on first run\n   152→- [ ] All SQL uses parameterized queries (grep for f-strings in db/)\n   153→- [ ] structlog outputs JSON logs\n   154→\n   155→---\n   156→\n   157→## Phase 2: Data Ingestion — Exchange & Derivatives\n   158→\n   159→### What to implement\n   160→1. **Exchange collector** (`ingest/exchange.py`):\n   161→   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_ohlcv('BTC/USDT:USDT', '1m')` for 1-min klines\n   162→   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_order_book('BTC/USDT:USDT', limit=20)` for depth snapshots\n   163→   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_trades('BTC/USDT:USDT')` for aggTrades\n   164→   - Store each to SQLite at configured intervals\n   165→\n   166→2. **Derivatives collector** (`ingest/derivatives.py`):\n   167→   - ccxt REST: `bybit.fetch_open_interest('BTC/USDT:USDT')` — poll every 5 min\n   168→   - ccxt REST: `bybit.fetch_funding_rate('BTC/USDT:USDT')` — poll every 5 min\n   169→   - Direct Bybit WebSocket: `allLiquidation.BTCUSDT` stream — real-time\n   170→   - Connection: `wss://stream.bybit.com/v5/public/linear`, subscribe `{\"op\":\"subscribe\",\"args\":[\"allLiquidation.BTCUSDT\"]}`\n   171→\n   172→3. **Orchestrator** (`ingest/orchestrator.py`):\n   173→   - Manages all collectors as async tasks\n   174→   - Handles reconnection, error logging, graceful shutdown\n   175→   - Health checks for each stream\n   176→\n   177→### Documentation references\n   178→- ccxt pro: `watch_order_book`, `watch_trades`, `watch_ohlcv` — batch_first pattern\n   179→- Bybit liquidation: `allLiquidation` topic (NOT deprecated `liquidation` topic)\n   180→- Bybit WS heartbeat: send `ping` every 20 seconds\n   181→\n   182→### Verification\n   183→- [ ] Run collectors for 10 minutes, verify data in SQLite\n   184→- [ ] Liquidation events appear when market is volatile\n   185→- [ ] OI and funding rate update every 5 minutes\n   186→- [ ] Reconnection works after simulated disconnect\n   187→- [ ] No duplicate records in database\n   188→\n   189→---\n   190→\n   191→## Phase 3: Data Ingestion — On-Chain & Cross-Market\n   192→\n   193→### What to implement\n   194→1. **On-chain collector** (`ingest/onchain.py`):\n   195→   - mempool.space WebSocket (`wss://mempool.space/api/v1/ws`):\n   196→     - Subscribe: `{\"action\":\"want\",\"data\":[\"blocks\",\"stats\"]}`\n   197→     - Subscribe: `{\"track-mempool\": true}` for all new txs\n   198→     - Client-side filter: flag transactions with output sum > 10 BTC as whale txs\n   199→   - Blockchair REST (polling every 60s):\n   200→     - `GET https://api.blockchair.com/bitcoin/mempool/transactions?q=output_total(1000000000..)&s=output_total(desc)`\n   201→     - Whale transactions > 10 BTC from mempool\n   202→   - Known exchange address monitoring:\n   203→     - Maintain a list of top 20 exchange cold/hot wallet addresses\n   204→     - Poll via mempool.space `/address/:address/txs` every 2 min\n   205→   - Alternative.me Fear & Greed: `GET https://api.alternative.me/fng/` — poll every 30 min\n   206→\n   207→2. **Cross-market collector** (`ingest/cross_market.py`):\n   208→   - ETH: ccxt pro `watch_ohlcv('ETH/USDT:USDT', '1m')` — real-time\n   209→   - NQ futures: yfinance `yf.download('NQ=F', interval='5m', period='5d')` — poll every 5 min\n   210→   - Gold: yfinance `yf.download('GC=F', interval='5m', period='5d')` — poll every 5 min\n   211→   - DXY: yfinance `yf.download('DX-Y.NYB', interval='5m', period='5d')` — poll every 5 min\n   212→   - Note: yfinance data is ~15 min delayed — acceptable for lead-lag detection (lag is minutes-to-hours)\n   213→\n   214→### Rate limit awareness\n   215→- Blockchair: max 30 req/min, 1,440/day — budget carefully\n   216→- mempool.space: no published limit, be respectful (1 WebSocket connection is fine)\n   217→- yfinance: no official limit, keep under 100 req/session\n   218→\n   219→### Verification\n   220→- [ ] Whale transactions detected and stored (check against whale-alert Twitter for validation)\n   221→- [ ] Mempool pressure metrics (size, fee rates) updating in real-time\n   222→- [ ] ETH price streaming alongside BTC\n   223→- [ ] NQ/Gold/DXY data updating every 5 min (with 15-min delay noted in metadata)\n   224→- [ ] Fear & Greed index stored with timestamps\n   225→\n   226→---\n   227→\n   228→## Phase 4: Feature Engineering — Microstructure Edge\n   229→\n   230→### What to implement\n   231→1. **Order book features** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   232→   - Bid-ask spread: `(best_ask - best_bid) / mid_price`\n   233→   - Order book imbalance (top 5 levels): `(bid_vol - ask_vol) / (bid_vol + ask_vol)`\n   234→   - Depth imbalance: weighted by price proximity to mid\n   235→   - Book pressure: ratio of volume within 0.1% of mid on each side\n   236→   - Spread velocity: rate of change of spread over last N snapshots\n   237→\n   238→2. **Trade flow features** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   239→   - Aggressive buy/sell ratio: classify trades by taker side from aggTrade `m` field (buyer is maker = sell aggression)\n   240→   - Trade intensity: trades per second, rolling 1-min and 5-min\n   241→   - Volume delta: cumulative (aggressive_buy_vol - aggressive_sell_vol)\n   242→   - Large trade detection: flag trades > 2 std devs above mean size\n   243→   - Trade clustering: count of trades in rapid succession (< 100ms apart)\n   244→\n   245→3. **Absorption detection** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   246→   - Price doesn't move despite large aggressive orders hitting one side\n   247→   - Measure: large volume delta without proportional price change\n   248→   - Signal: potential hidden liquidity / institutional activity\n   249→\n   250→### Documentation references\n   251→- Binance aggTrade `m` field: `true` = buyer is market maker (i.e., trade was a sell aggression)\n   252→- Order book from `watch_order_book`: `ob['bids']` = [[price, amount], ...], `ob['asks']` = [[price, amount], ...]\n   253→\n   254→### Verification\n   255→- [ ] Order book imbalance correlates with short-term price direction (basic sanity check)\n   256→- [ ] Volume delta calculation matches manual spot-check\n   257→- [ ] Features update in real-time as new data arrives\n   258→- [ ] No look-ahead bias in feature calculations (features only use data available at calculation time)\n   259→\n   260→---\n   261→\n   262→## Phase 5: Feature Engineering — On-Chain & Cross-Market Edges\n   263→\n   264→### What to implement\n   265→1. **On-chain features** (`features/onchain.py`):\n   266→   - Whale flow score: net BTC moved to/from exchange addresses in rolling 30-min window\n   267→   - Mempool pressure: mempool size rate of change, fee spike detection\n   268→   - Large tx momentum: count and total value of >10 BTC transactions in last 15 min\n   269→   - Exchange balance delta: change in known exchange address balances (approximation)\n   270→   - Fear & Greed momentum: rate of change of index (not raw value — everyone has raw value)\n   271→\n   272→2. **Cross-market features** (`features/cross_market.py`):\n   273→   - Lead-lag correlation: rolling Pearson correlation between BTC returns and NQ/Gold/DXY returns at various lags (0, 1, 2, 5, 10 min)\n   274→   - Dynamic lead-lag detection: which asset is currently leading? Use Granger causality test on rolling window\n   275→   - Divergence signals: BTC moving opposite to its current leader = mean reversion signal\n   276→   - ETH/BTC ratio momentum: rate of change of ETH/BTC price ratio (risk appetite proxy)\n   277→   - Cross-market volatility spillover: when NQ vol spikes, does BTC vol follow? Rolling correlation of volatility\n   278→\n   279→3. **Temporal features** (`features/temporal.py`):\n   280→   - Cyclical encoding: `sin(2π × minute/60)`, `cos(2π × minute/60)` for minute-of-hour\n   281→   - Same for hour-of-day, day-of-week\n   282→   - Session indicator: Asia (00-08 UTC), Europe (08-16 UTC), US (16-00 UTC)\n   283→   - Time-to-funding: minutes until next Bybit funding rate settlement (every 8h)\n   284→\n   285→4. **Technical features** (`features/technical.py`):\n   286→   - Using pandas-ta: RSI(14), MACD(12,26,9), Bollinger(20,2), ATR(14), VWAP\n   287→   - Volume: OBV, volume-weighted momentum, volume profile\n   288→   - Returns: 1m, 5m, 15m, 30m log returns and volatility\n   289→\n   290→5. **Feature pipeline** (`features/pipeline.py`):\n   291→   - Combines all feature sets into single DataFrame\n   292→   - Handles NaN filling (forward-fill for price, zero for counts)\n   293→   - Feature normalization (rolling z-score, not global — prevents look-ahead)\n   294→   - Outputs: feature matrix aligned to 5-min prediction intervals\n   295→\n   296→### Verification\n   297→- [ ] Lead-lag correlation shows NQ leading BTC during US session (known relationship)\n   298→- [ ] Whale flow features are non-zero during known large BTC movements\n   299→- [ ] Feature pipeline produces consistent output shape\n   300→- [ ] No NaN/Inf values in output\n   301→- [ ] Rolling z-score uses only past data (no future leakage)\n   302→\n   303→---\n   304→\n   305→## Phase 6: Regime Detection\n   306→\n   307→### What to implement\n   308→1. **HMM regime detector** (`regime/detector.py`):\n   309→   - Input features: log returns, realized volatility (12-period rolling std), volume change rate\n   310→   - Fit `GaussianHMM(n_components=3, covariance_type='full', n_iter=1000)` for 3 regimes\n   311→   - Label regimes post-hoc by characteristics:\n   312→     - Trending: high absolute returns, moderate volatility\n   313→     - Mean-reverting: low returns, low volatility\n   314→     - Volatile/chaotic: high volatility, mixed returns\n   315→   - Model selection: fit n=2,3,4,5 and select by BIC\n   316→   - Pseudo-incremental update: refit every 4 hours on sliding 7-day window with `init_params=\"\"`\n   317→\n   318→2. **Regime labels** (`regime/labels.py`):\n   319→   - Map HMM state indices to semantic labels (states are arbitrary numbers)\n   320→   - Sort by volatility: lowest vol state = mean-reverting, highest = volatile\n   321→   - Provide regime probability distribution (not just hard label)\n   322→   - Regime transition probability: extract from `model.transmat_` for \"regime about to change\" signal\n   323→\n   324→### Verification\n   325→- [ ] 3 distinct regimes visible when plotted against price history\n   326→- [ ] Regime labels are stable (same market conditions → same regime across refits)\n   327→- [ ] Regime transitions align with known market events (e.g., CPI releases, ETF approvals)\n   328→- [ ] Regime probabilities sum to 1.0\n   329→\n   330→---\n   331→\n   332→## Phase 7: Models — Direction & Magnitude\n   333→\n   334→### What to implement\n   335→1. **XGBoost direction classifier** (`models/xgb_direction.py`):\n   336→   - Target: 3-class classification (up > +0.1%, down < -0.1%, flat)\n   337→   - One model per regime (3 regimes × 1 XGBoost = 3 models)\n   338→   - Features: full feature pipeline output\n   339→   - Training: sliding window walk-forward, retrain every 24h on 14-day window\n   340→   - Incremental update: `model.fit(X_new, y_new, xgb_model=model.get_booster())`\n   341→   - Feature importance tracking: log top 20 features per regime per retrain\n   342→\n   343→2. **GRU magnitude predictor** (`models/gru_magnitude.py`):\n   344→   - Target: predicted 5-min return magnitude (regression)\n   345→   - One model per regime (3 regimes × 1 GRU = 3 models)\n   346→   - Architecture: `GRU(input_size=N, hidden_size=64, num_layers=2, batch_first=True)` → `Linear(64, 1)`\n   347→   - Sequence length: 24 steps (2 hours of 5-min candles) — tune with Optuna\n   348→   - Training: sliding window, retrain every 24h, gradient clipping at 1.0\n   349→   - Never shuffle DataLoader\n   350→\n   351→3. **Regime-routed ensemble** (`models/ensemble.py`):\n   352→   - Input: current regime (from Phase 6), feature matrix\n   353→   - Route to regime-specific XGBoost + GRU pair\n   354→   - XGBoost outputs: direction (up/down/flat) + confidence (probability)\n   355→   - GRU outputs: predicted return magnitude\n   356→   - Combined signal: `direction × magnitude × confidence`\n   357→   - Confidence threshold: only emit signal when XGBoost confidence > 0.6\n   358→   - Disagreement handling: if XGBoost says up but GRU predicts negative magnitude → no signal\n   359→\n   360→### Verification\n   361→- [ ] Each regime-specific model trained on filtered data (only samples from that regime)\n   362→- [ ] Walk-forward validation shows >52% directional accuracy (above random baseline)\n   363→- [ ] Feature importance differs meaningfully across regimes\n   364→- [ ] Ensemble disagreement rate is tracked and logged\n   365→- [ ] No look-ahead bias: verify test predictions only use training data available before test timestamp\n   366→\n   367→---\n   368→\n   369→## Phase 8: Hyperparameter Tuning\n   370→\n   371→### What to implement\n   372→1. **Optuna integration** (`models/tuning.py`):\n   373→   - XGBoost search space:\n   374→     ```python\n   375→     max_depth: suggest_int(3, 12)\n   376→     learning_rate: suggest_float(0.01, 0.3, log=True)\n   377→     min_child_weight: suggest_int(1, 250)\n   378→     subsample: suggest_float(0.5, 1.0)\n   379→     colsample_bytree: suggest_float(0.5, 1.0)\n   380→     reg_lambda: suggest_float(0.001, 25.0, log=True)\n   381→     reg_alpha: suggest_float(0.001, 25.0, log=True)\n   382→     ```\n   383→   - GRU search space:\n   384→     ```python\n   385→     hidden_size: suggest_int(32, 256)\n   386→     num_layers: suggest_int(1, 3)\n   387→     lr: suggest_float(1e-5, 1e-2, log=True)\n   388→     dropout: suggest_float(0.1, 0.5)\n   389→     seq_len: suggest_int(12, 60)\n   390→     ```\n   391→   - HMM: tune `n_components` (2-5) by BIC\n   392→   - Use `MedianPruner(n_startup_trials=5, n_warmup_steps=10)` for both\n   393→   - Use `XGBoostPruningCallback` for XGBoost specifically\n   394→   - Objective: maximize walk-forward Sharpe ratio (not just accuracy)\n   395→\n   396→2. **Feature selection via tsfresh** (offline, one-time):\n   397→   - Run `extract_features` with `EfficientFCParameters` on historical data\n   398→   - Identify top statistical features (autocorrelation lags, entropy, etc.)\n   399→   - Implement top 10-15 discovered features manually in the live feature pipeline\n   400→\n   401→### Verification\n   402→- [ ] Optuna study completes 50+ trials per model\n   403→- [ ] Best hyperparameters improve Sharpe over defaults\n   404→- [ ] Pruning correctly stops poor trials early\n   405→- [ ] tsfresh features that made the cut are documented\n   406→\n   407→---\n   408→\n   409→## Phase 9: Backtesting Framework\n   410→\n   411→### What to implement\n   412→1. **Walk-forward engine** (`backtest/walk_forward.py`):\n   413→   - Custom implementation (not just sklearn TimeSeriesSplit):\n   414→     ```python\n   415→     walk_forward_validate(X, y, model, train_size=4032, test_size=288, step_size=288, gap=1)\n   416→     # 4032 = 14 days of 5-min candles, 288 = 1 day, gap=1 to prevent leakage\n   417→     ```\n   418→   - Sliding window (not expanding) — crypto regimes shift too fast\n   419→   - Re-detect regime at each step\n   420→   - Retrain regime-specific models at each step\n   421→\n   422→2. **Execution simulator** (`backtest/simulator.py`):\n   423→   - Slippage model: 0.01-0.05% per trade (configurable)\n   424→   - Transaction fees: 0.04% maker / 0.06% taker (Binance futures)\n   425→   - Latency simulation: 50-200ms delay between signal and execution\n   426→   - Position sizing: Kelly criterion or fixed fractional\n   427→   - No trading during regime transitions (confidence < threshold)\n   428→\n   429→3. **Metrics** (`backtest/metrics.py`):\n   430→   - Directional accuracy (per regime)\n   431→   - Sharpe ratio (annualized)\n   432→   - Max drawdown\n   433→   - Profit factor\n   434→   - Win rate, average win/loss ratio\n   435→   - Calmar ratio\n   436→   - Trade count per day\n   437→   - Regime accuracy (predicted vs actual)\n   438→\n   439→### Verification\n   440→- [ ] Backtest on 30+ days of historical data\n   441→- [ ] Results include transaction costs (no \"zero-cost\" delusion)\n   442→- [ ] Sharpe > 0 after costs (basic sanity)\n   443→- [ ] Compare against baselines: buy-and-hold, momentum, random\n   444→- [ ] Metrics breakdown per regime shows which regimes are profitable\n   445→\n   446→---\n   447→\n   448→## Phase 10: API & Live Prediction\n   449→\n   450→### What to implement\n   451→1. **FastAPI server** (`api/server.py`):\n   452→   - `GET /predict` — returns current prediction (direction, magnitude, confidence, regime)\n   453→   - `GET /health` — checks all data streams are alive, models are loaded, last prediction timestamp\n   454→   - `GET /metrics` — live accuracy tracking, rolling Sharpe\n   455→   - `GET /regime` — current regime + transition probabilities\n   456→   - All responses include timestamps and staleness warnings\n   457→\n   458→2. **Live prediction loop** (`scripts/live.py`):\n   459→   - Async event loop running all collectors\n   460→   - Feature pipeline triggers on each new 5-min candle close\n   461→   - Regime detection updates\n   462→   - Model inference → prediction\n   463→   - Store prediction + actual outcome for live accuracy tracking\n   464→   - Auto-retrain models every 24h on latest data\n   465→\n   466→### Verification\n   467→- [ ] API responds in < 100ms\n   468→- [ ] Health endpoint actually checks dependencies (not just returns \"ok\")\n   469→- [ ] Predictions emit within 1 second of candle close\n   470→- [ ] Live accuracy tracking matches backtest expectations (within reason)\n   471→- [ ] Graceful degradation: if one data source fails, system still produces predictions (with lower confidence)\n   472→\n   473→---\n   474→\n   475→## Phase 11: Historical Backfill & Full Validation\n   476→\n   477→### What to implement\n   478→1. **Historical data collection** (`scripts/collect_history.py`):\n   479→   - Binance REST: fetch 30-60 days of 1-min OHLCV via `exchange.fetch_ohlcv()`\n   480→   - Bybit REST: backfill OI history (`fetch_open_interest_history`) and funding rate history\n   481→   - yfinance: backfill NQ, Gold, DXY 5-min data (limited to 60 days)\n   482→   - Note: order book and trade-level data cannot be backfilled — microstructure features start from collection date\n   483→\n   484→2. **Full system validation**:\n   485→   - Run complete pipeline: ingest → features → regime → models → backtest\n   486→   - Compare regime detection against known market events\n   487→   - Validate that each edge contributes independently (ablation study):\n   488→     - Model with all features vs model without microstructure\n   489→     - Model with all features vs model without on-chain\n   490→     - Model with all features vs model without cross-market\n   491→     - Model with all features vs model without regime routing\n   492→\n   493→### Verification\n   494→- [ ] Each edge shows positive marginal contribution in ablation study\n   495→- [ ] Full system Sharpe > any single-edge system\n   496→- [ ] No edge has negative contribution (remove if so)\n   497→- [ ] System handles missing data gracefully (e.g., no on-chain data for first 30 days)\n   498→\n   499→---\n   500→\n   501→## Execution Order & Dependencies\n   502→\n   503→```\n   504→Phase 1 (Foundation)\n   505→  ↓\n   506→Phase 2 (Exchange Ingestion) ──────┐\n   507→  ↓                                 │\n   508→Phase 3 (On-Chain + Cross-Market) ─┤\n   509→  ↓                                 │\n   510→Phase 4 (Microstructure Features) ──┤── can partially parallelize\n   511→  ↓                                 │\n   512→Phase 5 (On-Chain + Cross Features)┘\n   513→  ↓\n   514→Phase 6 (Regime Detection)\n   515→  ↓\n   516→Phase 7 (Models)\n   517→  ↓\n   518→Phase 8 (Tuning)\n   519→  ↓\n   520→Phase 9 (Backtesting)\n   521→  ↓\n   522→Phase 10 (API + Live)\n   523→  ↓\n   524→Phase 11 (Validation + Ablation)\n   525→```\n   526→\n   527→Phases 2-5 can overlap: start collecting data in Phase 2-3 while building features in Phase 4-5. Models (Phase 7) need data from all feature phases.\n   528→\n   529→---\n   530→\n   531→## Key Design Decisions\n   532→\n   533→1. **Sliding window, not expanding** — crypto non-stationarity means old data hurts more than helps\n   534→2. **Per-regime models** — a trending market model is useless in a ranging market\n   535→3. **Confidence gating** — no signal is better than a low-confidence signal\n   536→4. **Magnitude + direction separation** — XGBoost excels at classification, GRU at regression\n   537→5. **15-min delay on cross-market is acceptable** — the lead-lag relationship operates on minutes-to-hours, not seconds\n   538→6. **No exchange flow data** — no free API exists; we approximate via address monitoring\n   539→7. **SQLite for dev** — zero setup, switch to TimescaleDB when moving to production\n   540→8. **Feature normalization via rolling z-score** — prevents global normalization look-ahead bias\n   541→"}]},"uuid":"f997e255-13ce-4794-a0db-fd5060287ce7","timestamp":"2026-03-23T11:59:32.602Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"85ae49fc-f0d8-4a88-b41e-49f974b799f0","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

{"parentUuid":"4ffdf161-1939-4506-aaa9-578889e1194c","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"bf69de4e-ca7c-4b8d-979b-5b0fcb3d2ef3","agentId":"ad606be3552d63ad7","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01UtP3DkiCgf7rrSKMjBJp5R","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Research Synthesis: Key Findings & Plan Revisions\n     2→\n     3→> 20 research agents, 21 reports, ~500K words of analysis. This document distills the critical findings that change how we build the system.\n     4→\n     5→---\n     6→\n     7→## Critical Reality Checks\n     8→\n     9→### The Hard Numbers\n    10→- **Realistic directional accuracy**: 52-56% at 5-min (not 60%+)\n    11→- **Backtest-to-live degradation**: 50-70% (a Sharpe 2.0 backtest → Sharpe 0.6-1.0 live)\n    12→- **Round-trip costs**: 8-12 bps minimum (taker fee + slippage)\n    13→- **Minimum gross return per trade**: >15 bps to be profitable after costs\n    14→- **Alpha half-life in crypto**: 1-6 months for ML-based patterns\n    15→- **Optimal feature count**: 18-25 (not 200+)\n    16→- **Monthly infra cost**: $40-100 (minimum viable)\n    17→\n    18→### What We Got Wrong in V1 Plan\n    19→1. **XGBoost → LightGBM** — LightGBM outperforms XGBoost on 5-min crypto by 0.5-1.5%\n    20→2. **LSTM → GRU + TCN** — GRU trains 20-40% faster, comparable accuracy. TCN is parallelizable and competitive.\n    21→3. **3 regime-specific models → hierarchical ensemble** — regime detection should be a feature, not model routing (too few samples per regime)\n    22→4. **On-chain as primary signal → on-chain as regime context only** — academic evidence shows on-chain signals operate at 4h-24h, NOT 5-min\n    23→5. **Sentiment analysis → skip for 5-min** — too slow. Funding rate is the only useful \"sentiment\" at this timeframe\n    24→6. **Most TA indicators → noise at 5-min** — MACD, Bollinger, Ichimoku, etc. are useless. Only RSI (with regime filter), short ROC, and ATR survive\n    25→\n    26→---\n    27→\n    28→## 5 Highest-Impact Changes to the Plan\n    29→\n    30→### 1. Core Model: LightGBM + Stacking Ensemble (not XGBoost per-regime)\n    31→\n    32→**Old plan**: 3 XGBoost classifiers (one per regime) + 3 GRU regressors\n    33→**New plan**:\n    34→- LightGBM (primary classifier) + CatBoost (secondary) + GRU (temporal features)\n    35→- Stacking meta-learner (logistic regression) combines them\n    36→- Single model set, not per-regime (regime becomes a feature input)\n    37→- Add LightGBM quantile regression (5 quantiles) for risk assessment\n    38→\n    39→**Why**: Per-regime models fragment already-scarce data. A single ensemble with regime features is more robust. Stacking is the #1 gain after feature engineering (Kaggle consensus + financial ML literature).\n    40→\n    41→### 2. Feature Priority: Microstructure First, Everything Else Second\n    42→\n    43→**Research consensus**: OFI + OBI + microprice capture 60-80% of achievable 5-min signal.\n    44→\n    45→**Tier 1 (must-have, ~15 features)**:\n    46→- Order book imbalance (weighted, levels 1-3 and 1-5)\n    47→- Trade flow imbalance (30s and 5min windows)\n    48→- Bid-ask spread (relative)\n    49→- Volume delta (1-bar, 5-bar)\n    50→- Volume rate of change\n    51→- VWAP deviation (1hr)\n    52→- Realized vol (5-min, 30-min)\n    53→- Parkinson vol (30-min)\n    54→- ROC (1, 3, 6, 12 bars)\n    55→\n    56→**Tier 2 (strong additions, ~10 features)**:\n    57→- Book depth ratio, pressure gradient\n    58→- Trade arrival rate\n    59→- EWMA volatility, vol-of-vol\n    60→- RSI(14), linear regression slope(20)\n    61→- Price quantile rank(60)\n    62→\n    63→**Tier 3 (context, ~5 features)**:\n    64→- Hour-of-day (sin/cos)\n    65→- Funding rate\n    66→- Spread × OBI interaction\n    67→- NQ 5-min returns (lagged 1-3 bars) — during US hours only\n    68→- VIX level (regime classifier)\n    69→\n    70→### 3. Confidence Gating Pipeline (2-4x Sharpe improvement)\n    71→\n    72→The full gating pipeline is the single biggest Sharpe multiplier:\n    73→\n    74→```\n    75→Raw Prediction → Calibration (isotonic) → Meta-Labeling Gate → Ensemble Agreement Check → Conformal Prediction Gate → Signal Filters (vol, regime, liquidity) → Adaptive Threshold → Drawdown Gate → Position Sizing (quarter-Kelly) → EXECUTE or ABSTAIN\n    76→```\n    77→\n    78→Key layers:\n    79→- **Meta-labeling**: Secondary model predicts \"will THIS trade be profitable?\" — Lopez de Prado's technique, 50-100% Sharpe improvement\n    80→- **Conformal prediction**: Prediction set must be singleton {UP} or {DOWN}, not {UP, DOWN}\n    81→- **Adaptive threshold**: Regime-dependent, updated weekly via rolling Sharpe optimization\n    82→- **Drawdown gate**: Progressive position reduction 3%→15%, graduated re-entry\n    83→\n    84→### 4. Regime Detection: Hierarchical Ensemble (not just HMM)\n    85→\n    86→**Old plan**: Single 3-state HMM\n    87→**New plan**: 4-layer hierarchy\n    88→\n    89→| Layer | Method | Update Frequency | Purpose |\n    90→|-------|--------|-----------------|---------|\n    91→| Fast (every bar) | Efficiency Ratio + GARCH vol | O(1) | Quick regime estimate |\n    92→| Core (every bar) | 2-state HMM (filtered probs) + BOCPD | O(K²) | State identification + change detection |\n    93→| Slow (hourly) | Rolling Hurst (24h DFA) | O(window) | Trending vs mean-reverting context |\n    94→| Meta (weekly refit) | LightGBM on all above | Batch | Optimal regime label |\n    95→\n    96→**Why**: BOCPD detects changes 2-10 bars faster than HMM alone. Efficiency Ratio is the highest signal-to-complexity feature for trend vs range. Hurst provides macro context.\n    97→\n    98→### 5. Event-Driven Macro Module (Highest Single Edge)\n    99→\n   100→**New finding**: NQ reaction to macro events (CPI, FOMC) leads BTC by 2-5 minutes with ~62-68% accuracy.\n   101→\n   102→```\n   103→T+0s:     CPI/FOMC released\n   104→T+0-60s:  NQ/ES reacts\n   105→T+2-5m:   BTC follows NQ direction (~65% of the time)\n   106→```\n   107→\n   108→**Implementation**:\n   109→- Pre-scheduled macro calendar\n   110→- At T+0: monitor NQ 5-min return direction\n   111→- At T+2min: enter BTC in NQ's direction\n   112→- At T+5-10min: exit (mean reversion risk)\n   113→- VIX-gated: skip when VIX > 35\n   114→\n   115→This is orthogonal to the ML model and can run as an independent alpha source.\n   116→\n   117→---\n   118→\n   119→## Revised Architecture\n   120→\n   121→```\n   122→┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n   123→│                   DATA LAYER                         │\n   124→├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n   125→│ Binance WS: klines, depth@100ms, aggTrades          │\n   126→│ Bybit WS: allLiquidation, funding (REST)            │\n   127→│ Cross-market: NQ (yfinance/TwelveData), ETH (ccxt)  │\n   128→│ On-chain: mempool.space WS (whale detection only)    │\n   129→│ Macro: economic calendar (scheduled events)          │\n   130→└────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────┘\n   131→                     │\n   132→                     ▼\n   133→┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n   134→│               FEATURE ENGINE                         │\n Aggressive limit order (1-2 ticks inside)            │\n   182→│ 10s timeout → convert to market order                │\n   183→│ 5-30s entry delay for better fills                   │\n   184→│ percentile, funding z-score,            │\n   205→│   liquidation burst rate, book depth, price velocity │\n   206→│ Hawkes process for cascade intensity                 │\n   207→│ Output: cascade Component | V1 Plan | V2 (Post-Research) | Why Changed |\n   216→|-----------|---------|-------------------|-------------|\n   217→| Primary model | XGBoost | **LightGBM** | Faster, +0.5-1.5% accuracy on crypto |\n   218→| Secondary model | — | **CatBoost** | Ordered boosting prevents leakage, diversity |\n   219→| Sequence model | GRU | **GRU + TCN** | TCN is parallelizable, competitive |\n   220→| Ensemble | Simple combination | **Stacking** | 2-5% over best single model |\n   221→| Regime detection | 3-state HMM | **Hierarchical** (HMM + BOCPD + GARCH + ER) | Faster detection, more robust |\n   222→| Feature library | pandas-ta | **numpy-native** | 10-50x faster on hot path |\n   223→| Normalization | Rolling z-score | **Dual pipeline** (raw for trees, robust for neural) | Trees harmed by normalization |\n   224→| Target | Binary (up/down) | **Ternary** (up/flat/down) with adaptive threshold | Acknowledges untradeable periods |\n   225→| Calibration | — | **Isotonic + Venn-Abers** | Required for confidence gating |\n   226→| Position sizing | Fixed fractional | **Quarter-Kelly × confidence** | Research-backed optimal sizing |\n   227→| Sentiment | Twitter NLP + Fear&Greed | **Funding rate only** | All other sentiment too slow for 5-min |\n   228→| On-chain | Primary signal | **Regime context only** | Operates at 4h-24h, not 5-min |\n   229→| Data structures | pandas DataFrames | **Numpy ring buffers** | 10-20x less memory |\n   230→| Tick storage | SQLite | **SQLite dev → TimescaleDB prod** | (unchanged, confirmed by research) |\n   231→| Model inference | Native Python | **ONNX Runtime** | 2-5x speedup |\n   232→\n   233→---\n   234→\n   235→## Revised Phase Plan\n   236→\n   237→### Phase 1: Foundation (unchanged)\n   238→Project setup, uv, SQLite, structlog, config via Pydantic Settings + Doppler.\n   239→\n   240→### Phase 2: Data Ingestion — Exchange & Derivatives\n   241→- Add Binance `!forceOrder@arr` for liquidation stream (not just Bybit)\n   242→- Add Binance `depth@100ms` (not just depth20)\n   243→- Collect aggTrades for trade flow features\n   244→\n   245→### Phase 3: Data Ingestion — Cross-Market & Events\n   246→- **Downgrade on-chain**: Mempool monitoring for whale detection only (>10 BTC to known exchange)\n   247→- **Add macro calendar**: Pre-scheduled CPI/FOMC/NFP dates with NQ monitoring\n   248→- **Add VIX**: yfinance or Twelve Data for VIX level (regime classifier)\n   249→- **ETH**: ccxt WebSocket (unchanged)\n   250→\n   251→### Phase 4: Feature Engineering — Microstructure (HIGHEST PRIORITY)\n   252→- OBI (weighted, multi-level)\n   253→- OFI (Cont-Stoikov-Talreja model, multi-level)\n   254→- Microprice (Gatheral-Stoikov)\n   255→- Trade flow imbalance\n   256→- Absorption detection\n   257→- Kyle's Lambda (rolling, as conditioning variable)\n   258→\n   259→### Phase 5: Feature Engineering — Volume, Volatility, Momentum\n   260→- Volume delta (buy-sell), VWAP deviation, rate-of-change\n   261→- Realized vol, Parkinson, EWMA, vol-of-vol\n   262→- ROC at multiple lookbacks (1, 3, 6, 12 bars)\n   263→- RSI(14), linear regression slope(20), price quantile rank\n   264→- Dual normalization pipeline (raw for trees, robust scaling for neural)\n   265→\n   266→### Phase 6: Regime Detection — Hierarchical Ensemble\n   267→- Efficiency Ratio (fast, every bar)\n   268→- GJR-GARCH(1,1)-t conditional vol (fast, every bar)\n   269→- 2-state GaussianHMM (core, every bar, refit weekly)\n   270→- BOCPD change point detection (early warning)\n   271→- Rolling Hurst (slow, hourly)\n   272→- LightGBM meta-learner on regime features\n   273→\n   274→### Phase 7: Models — Stacking Ensemble\n   275→- LightGBM classifier (ternary target, adaptive threshold)\n   276→- CatBoost classifier (diversity through ordered boosting)\n   277→- GRU feature extractor → hidden state feeds into LightGBM\n   278→- LightGBM quantile regression (10th, 25th, 50th, 75th, 90th)\n   279→- Stacking meta-learner (logistic regression on OOF predictions)\n   280→- Isotonic regression calibration on held-out calibration set\n   281→\n   282→### Phase 8: Confidence Gating Pipeline\n   283→- Meta-labeling (primary ensemble → meta-model → trade gate)\n   284→- Ensemble agreement scoring\n   285→- Conformal prediction (adaptive α)\n   286→- Signal filters (vol range, regime stability, liquidity, news events)\n   287→- Adaptive confidence threshold (regime-dependent, weekly update)\n   288→- Drawdown gate (progressive reduction)\n   289→- Quarter-Kelly position sizing × composite confidence\n   290→\n   291→### Phase 9: Hyperparameter Tuning\n   292→- Optuna with MedianPruner\n   293→- Objective: walk-forward Sharpe (not accuracy)\n   294→- Deflated Sharpe Ratio to account for multiple trials\n   295→- Feature importance stability check across folds\n   296→\n   297→### Phase 10: Backtesting Framework\n   298→- Walk-forward with purging and embargo (gap = max feature 78→\n    79→    Args:\n    80→        returns: Per-bar log returns of the strategy (already position-weighted).\n    81→        positions: Position signal per bar (-1, 0, or +1). 10_000)\n    96→    net_returns = returns - cost_per_bar\n    97→\n    98→    # --- Sharpe ratio (annualized) ---\n    99→    excess = net_returns - RISK_FREE_PER_BAR\n   100→    sharpe =   144→        avg_bars_in_trade = float(np.mean([t[\"bars\"] for t in trades]))\n   145→    else:\n   146→        win_rate = 0.0\n   147→        avg_trade_return = 0.0\n   148→        avg_win = 0.0\n 181→        return 0.0\n   182→    return float(mean / std * np.sqrt(BARS_PER_YEAR))\n   183→\n   184→\n   185→def _max_drawdown_duration(cumulative: pd.Series) -> int:\n   186→    \"\"\"Longest streak (in bars) below the running maximum.\"\"\"\n   187→    running_max = cumulative.cummax()\n   188→    in_drawdown = cumulative < running_max\n   189→    if not in_drawdown.any():\n   190→ This technique can significantly reduce training time in your model updates.\n\n## Using init_model Parameter\n\nThe init_model parameter accepts a filename of LightGBM model or Booster instance used for continue training. This is the core mechanism for warm-starting your training.\n\n**Important Considerations:**\n\n- The keep_training_booster parameter controls whether the returned Booster will be used to keep training. If False, the returned value will be converted into _InnerPredictor before returning, meaning you won't be able to use eval, eval_train or eval_valid methods of the returned Booster.\n\n- When your model is very large and causes a memory error, you can try to set keep_training_booster to True to avoid the model conversion. You can still use _InnerPredictor as init_model for future continue training.\n\n## Warm-Start Challenges\n\nResearch indicates there are potential pitfalls with warm-starting: warm-starting from a pre-trained checkpoint, which is trained by partial data, leads to a lower accuracy than training the model from random initialization. To mitigate this, several weight reinitialization methods have been proposed, with the key being to forget partial of the learned knowledge selectively.\n\nThe search results provide technical details about the `init_model` parameter, but offer limited specific best practices documentation. For detailed implementation examples, you may want to check the LightGBM examples directory and community resources on incremental learning patterns.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"4fb523ae-d5ca-4763-aee9-3bec98de91a7","timestamp":"2026-03-23T12:00:38.982Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"651447bc-b985-4e6c-b3a4-be1f26a1b85c","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

Here's a summary of the relevant findings:\n\n## Key Results\n\nThe search returned comprehensive resources on model retraining pipelines, sliding vs. expanding windows, and practical implementation considerations—particularly in production ML and cryptocurrency trading contexts.\n\n**Sliding vs. Expanding Windows:**\n\nYou can either expand the training window to include all historical data (e.g., 2016-2018 expanding window) and predict for future periods, or maintain a fixed training window (e.g., 2017-2018 sliding window) and train different models for each prediction period. It's valuable to test both the sliding and expanding window approaches and then assess how models trained using both methods perform.\n\n**Retraining Strategies:**\n\nRetraining strategies can be categorized as scheduled (at fixed intervals), performance-based (triggered when metrics fall below thresholds), or continuous learning (constantly updating with new data in real-time or near-real-time).\n\n**Crypto Trading Implementation:**\n\nOne implementation choice for cryptocurrency models involves retraining weekly while tracking training dates per symbol, since different coins enter the trading universe at different times. For cryptocurrency models, expanding-window validation (training on 175 days, validating on the next 75 days, sliding forward) prevents look-ahead bias, rather than using random cross-validation.\n\n**Production Considerations:**\n\nModel drift and new data will always dictate that models are retrained to benefit from data freshness and new patterns, so having a robust model training pipeline curated with care is essential.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"86aa91a2-5725-4402-a0be-c5fbf58ae824","timestamp":"2026-03-23T12:00:39.078Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"b967ebe7-28d9-49bc-8240-441b1cfdd5a0","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

Here are the key findings:\n\n## What is PSI?\n\nPSI is a univariate drift metric that quantifies how much a variable's distribution has shifted between a baseline population (often model development or training data) and a comparison population (often recent scoring/production data). PSI is a widely used tool for detecting data drift, helping organizations monitor shifts in data distributions over time.\n\n## PSI Threshold Interpretations\n\nThe most commonly cited threshold rules of thumb are:\n\n- PSI less than 0.1 means the actual and expected distributions are considered similar, while PSI between 0.1 and 0.2 means the actual distribution is considered moderately different from the expected distribution\n- PSI beyond 0.2 is highly advised to develop a new model on a more recent sample\n\nAlternative thresholds mentioned include PSI < 0.1 (no significant change), 0.1 <= PSI < 0.25 (minor shift requiring attention), and PSI >= 0.25 (major shift requiring investigation and likely action).\n\n## Retraining Triggers\n\nPSI should be combined with outcome/performance monitoring (AUC, log loss, lift, calibration) to decide when to retrain vs. when to recalibrate thresholds. PSI calculates the data drift by comparing 2 populations (generally training data and inferencing data) to decide if there is need to retrain the model or not.\n\n## Practical Applications\n\nIn model monitoring, PSI is commonly applied to both model inputs (features) and model outputs (scores) to detect changes that may be associated with performance degradation or changing population characteristics.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"9cd616e7-4c77-4df7-b764-3b120a228fd6","timestamp":"2026-03-23T12:00:50.777Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e3f0c8c4-c9f0-4890-bdc5-cbbc56f9b583","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

The process involves the current production model, known as the \"champion,\" competing against one or more \"challengers,\" or newly proposed models.\n\nA/B testing splits a portion of the inference requests between the champion model and the one or more challengers through a randomly weighted step, with each model receiving inputs that are approximately proportional to the weight it is assigned.\n\n### Shadow Mode Deployment\n\nIn a shadow deployment, every model in your experimental pipeline receives the same data input, and all their inferences are logged, but the only model that actually influences the real-world decisions or outputs is the default model, often referred to as the \"champion,\" while the rest operate in the background.\n\nThe primary advantage of this method is that it allows for extensive testing and validation of a new model's performance and accuracy without any risk to the current system's stability or output quality, which is particularly valuable for \"sanity checking\" a model before it goes fully live.\n\n### Champion/Challenger Pattern\n\nChampion/challenger is a method that allows different approaches to testing predictive models in a production environment, similar to A/B testing from a marketing perspective, and enables you to both monitor and measure predictions using different variations of the same decision logic.\n\nDataRobot's capability enables customers, within a governed framework, to run their challenger models in shadow mode, alongside their current best performing model.\n\n### Key Differences\n\nWith A/B testing, you cannot compare a maximum accuracy model because you are often prohibited from putting that challenger model into a production environment, while shadowing lets you safely mirror before taking an approach that impacts your business or customers.\n\nThe search results provide detailed guidance on implementing these validation strategies effectively in production ML systems.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"b5e8dd8f-5152-47c3-a94a-66629a784c40","timestamp":"2026-03-23T12:00:54.377Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"2af2a97e-945d-44d8-80ff-515c63776643","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

Model rollback is the ability to quickly revert to a previous version of a machine learning model when the current version causes problems, which is critical for production ML systems where model failures can directly impact revenue, user experience, or safety.\n\n**Canary Deployment Strategy:**\nThe canary release strategy exposes the new model to a very small, controlled subset of live traffic (e.g., 1% or 5%), with metrics closely monitored for degradation in performance or error rates before a full rollout.\n\n**Model Registry:**\nTools like MLflow Model Registry, DVC, Weights & Biases, Kubeflow, Vertex AI, and SageMaker manage model versioning and rollback in production. A centralized registry maintains model states (Staging, Production, Archived), with only \"Production\" models served, helping teams know which model is live and who approved it.\n\n**Automated Rollback:**\nAutomated rollback is a crucial safety measure—if monitoring detects sharp degradation in latency or a sudden drop in prediction confidence, the system automatically kills the new model deployment and reverts all traffic to the last stable, archived model version.\n\n**Practical Implementation:**\nModels live in a registry with pinned digests, and rollback becomes: flip policy → revert threshold → pin old model, taking only seconds rather than hours.\n\nThe search results provide comprehensive coverage of these deployment patterns with practical implementation details for trading and production systems.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"cf5c2412-0593-4ea5-9ba6-69ce3a427caa","timestamp":"2026-03-23T12:01:06.934Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"bf57e8aa-1dd7-4f2a-b123-84b3c6a26476","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

Here's a summary of the key findings:\n\n## Model Decay and Feature Drift\n\nMachine learning model decay refers to the gradual performance degradation of a deployed model over time. Data drift is one of the primary causes of model decay, occurring when the statistical properties of input data change after deployment.\n\n## Feature Monitoring and Stability\n\nAutomated monitoring systems continuously track model performance and feature stability, with thresholds set for various metrics such as accuracy, KSTest, and PSI. The shadow feature comparison technique assesses feature stability by benchmarking original features against randomly generated shadow features, eliminating any feature that is less significant than its shadow counterparts.\n\n## Retraining Strategies\n\nOnce model performance falls below a certain threshold or a data shift is observed, a trigger can be set to retrain the model with recent data. Depending on the domain, you may need to retrain weekly, monthly, or quarterly, using a rolling window of the most recent data to maintain relevance while balancing between adapting to new trends and retaining long-term patterns.\n\n## Handling Feature Drift\n\nConsider re-designing a feature set if the features' characteristics change or you find some features unstable. Feature dropping is a simple but effective method to handle concept drift, where multiple models are trained using one feature at a time, and if a feature's AUC-ROC response goes beyond a certain threshold, it can be dropped as it might participate in drifting.\n\n## Alternative Approaches\n\nEnsemble approaches combine multiple models trained on different time periods, reducing sensitivity to any single drift pattern, with the ensemble automatically weighting models showing better recent performance. A dual-model setup can be used where a first ML model uses only stable, reliable features and a second ML model corrects the output of the first using the bigger feature set.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"a06c05ab-8a4c-4666-95d1-038996f845dd","timestamp":"2026-03-23T12:01:07.280Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"1f46003a-f84b-422d-ad5a-1076ac0a7613","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

This counterintuitive finding suggests that the conventional wisdom about frequent retraining may not always be optimal.\n\n## Rolling Sharpe Ratio as a Trigger Mechanism\n\nA 12-month rolling Sharpe can be monitored by calculating monthly returns, subtracting a constant risk-free rate, then dividing by the 12-month standard deviation of those excess returns, with the result updating each month for a fresh risk-adjusted performance number.\n\nA practical retraining trigger can be established: Set a stop-loss guideline based on rolling 12-month Sharpe, where if an ETF's Sharpe falls more than 0.2 points from its current level, consider exiting the position.\n\n## Avoiding Overfitting Through Framework Design\n\nWalk-forward validation frameworks employ rolling window validation across multiple independent test periods and enforce strict information set discipline to mitigate overfitting and lookahead bias.\n\n## Sharpe Ratio Threshold Calibration\n\nThe benchmark Sharpe ratio is user-defined; researchers aiming for strategies with at least SR of 1.5 can set the benchmark to 1 or 1.5. {"parentUuid":"0099c6fc-e2bc-494c-b8ab-773d26c78885","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"2c82d7a3-137f-4ebd-9043-1e4ab139ca6a","agentId":"ad606be3552d63ad7","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01GoUzYXaeaN4cjA6YbkF363","type":"tool_result","content":"# Handling Drifting Features in ML Model Maintenance\n\n## Key Decision Framework\n\nRather than automatically discarding drifting features, the article recommends a structured evaluation approach:\n\n### 1. **Assess Feature Selection Rigor**\nIf your model is in a \"quick-and-dirty\" phase with minimal feature engineering, removing low-quality features is reasonable. However, if features were carefully selected, investigate further before removal.\n\n### 2. **Evaluate Feature Importance**\n- **Unimportant drifting features**: Safe to drop or exclude from monitoring\n- **Critical features**: Cannot eliminate; instead investigate the \"real-world phenomenon\" behind the drift\n\n### 3. **Consider Dual-Model Architecture**\nBuild a primary model using stable features and a secondary model to refine predictions using volatile features. This balances reliability with performance.\n\n### 4. **Check for Seasonality**\nThe drift may reflect temporal patterns rather than true distribution shifts. Adjust comparison windows accordingly or create separate models for different conditions (e.g., weather-based).\n\n### 5. **Apply Contextual Judgment**\nThe recommendation emphasizes that \"there is no such thing as absolute drift.\" Drift detection serves as a heuristic—not a definitive signal for action.
